NMAAHC

Ticket link: https://nmaahc.si.edu/visit/plan-your-visit 
Admissions info: 
Free Timed-Entry Passes 
All visitors, regardless of age, must have a timed-entry pass to enter the museum.
A limited number of timed-entry passes are available.
Advance timed-entry passes are released 30 days in advance on a rolling basis.
Same-day timed-entry passes are released online only by 8:15 a.m. EST daily.
Timed-entry passes may not be sold or transferred and are for personal use only.
Individuals can reserve up to nine free timed-entry passes for their visit. For groups of 10 or more, please reserve group passes.
We are honored to welcome veterans, active-duty personnel, and first responders to the museum. You do not need to register for a timed entry pass in advance. Upon arrival, you will simply present a valid military or work ID badge and complete a brief registration form for entry. You may bring up to 4 guests.
Please note: museum entry is subject to building capacity; weekends and holidays are peak visitation times. If the museum is at or near capacity, all visitors standing in line will be asked to wait until the museum has room to accommodate them. 
Additional Information 
All children (under the age of 18)тАпmustтАпbe accompanied by an adult chaperone. When accompanying children, one (1) adult can chaperone up to aтАпmaximumтАпof ten (10) children.тАп
Timed-entry passes are valid only for the issued date. Passes are void if altered.
Visitors can print timed-entry passes at home or present them on a mobile device. All passes will be scanned prior to entering the museum on Madison Drive or Constitution Ave.
If you cannot visit the museum on your scheduled date, please email NMAAHCVisitorServices@si.edu to return or exchange your passes.
Register or log in to your Smithsonian account to access and manage your free timed-entry passes.

Cultural Expressions
Permanent Exhibit (no end date)
Level 4 (L4), Culture Galleries
Cultural Expressions is a circular, experiential, introductory space to African American and African diaspora culture. Cultural Expressions highlights the central role of African American culture in everyday life, from food and fashion to music and language.
https://nmaahc.si.edu/explore/exhibitions/cultural-expressions 

Musical Crossroads
Permanent Exhibit (no end date)
Level 4 (L4), Culture Galleries
Musical Crossroads tells the story of African American music from the arrival of the first Africans to the present day. Musical Crossroads is the space where history and culture intermingle, where music serves as the crossroads between the interpretation of musical styles and traditions and the stories of cultural survivals, individual accomplishments, and social progress.
https://nmaahc.si.edu/explore/exhibitions/musical-crossroads 

Taking the Stage
Long-term Exhibit
Level 4 (L4), Culture Galleries
Taking the Stage explores the history of African Americans in theater, film, and television to celebrate their creative achievements, demonstrate their cultural impact, and illuminate their struggles for artistic freedom and equal representation.Throughout the exhibition, visitors see how African Americans have acted to shape and transform the ways they are represented onstage by challenging racial discrimination and stereotypes and producing more diverse images of African American identity and experience. Together these stories suggest how, in taking the stage to express their creative talents, artistic visions, and cultural identities, African Americans have been a force for freedom and social change.
https://nmaahc.si.edu/explore/exhibitions/taking-stage 

Making a Way Out of No Way
Permanent Exhibit (no end date)
Level 3 (L3), Community Galleries 
Taking its inspiration from a popular African American expression, Making a Way Out of No Way explores themes of agency, creativity, and resilience through personal stories of African Americans who challenged racial oppression and discrimination and created ways out of тАЬno way.тАЭ Through community institutions and activism, African Americans crafted possibilities in a world that denied them opportunities.
https://nmaahc.si.edu/explore/exhibitions/making-way-out-no-way 

Double Victory
Permanent Exhibit (no end date)
Level 3 (L3), General Colin L. Powell Gallery
Double Victory: The African American Military Experience conveys a sense of appreciation and respect for the military service of African Americans from the American Revolution to the War on Terror. In choosing to serve in the military, African Americans sought to have their service understood by the nation as a demand for liberty and citizenship. African American men and women who engaged in the military made their service useful not only for the good of their country, but to benefit both their personal lives and their community.
https://nmaahc.si.edu/explore/exhibitions/double-victory 
Power of Place
Permanent Exhibit (no end date)
Level 3 (L3), Community Galleries 
Power of Place explores stories of place from across the nation and the African American experience. People make places even as places change people. Places are secured by individual and collective struggle and spirit. Place is about movement, migration, and displacement. Place is where culture is made, traditions and histories are kept and lost, and identities are created, tested, and reshaped over time.
https://nmaahc.si.edu/explore/exhibitions/power-place 

Sports
Permanent Exhibit (no end date)
Level 3 (L3), Community Galleries
Sports: Leveling the Playing Field explores the contributions of athletes, both on and off the field. Some athletes have been symbolic figures of Black ability, while others have taken their activism beyond the court to the courtroom, boardroom and the newsroom. Because sports were among the first, and most high profile spaces to accept African Americans on relative terms of equality, sport has had a unique role within American culture. Within black communities, sports have always been political. From the refusal to allow African Americans an opportunity to compete to the formation of African American segregated sporting teams and leagues; from the hard won battles to compete at the highest levels of the game to the introduction of African American expressive cultural practices within the games, the African American presence in sports has had social and political consequences.
https://nmaahc.si.edu/explore/exhibitions/sports 

Explore More!
Permanent Exhibit (no end date)
Level 2 (L2), Target Learning Center, Earl W. and Amanda Stafford Center for African American Media Arts and Robert Frederick Smith Explore Your Family History Center
Explore More! is an interactive, multifaceted educational space dedicated to helping visitors connect and engage with African American history and culture in ways that expand perspectives, spark curiosity and creativity, and increase knowledge. 
https://nmaahc.si.edu/explore/exhibitions/explore-more 


Spirit in the Dark
NOV 18 2022 - MAR 2027
Level 2 (L2), Earl W. and Amanda Stafford Center for African American Media Arts (CAAMA) Gallery
Spirit in the Dark examines Black religious life through a selection of photographs from the Johnson Publishing Company, publisher of Ebony, Jet and Negro Digest. Diverse aspects of the Black religious experience are revealed through photographs and stories.
https://nmaahc.si.edu/explore/exhibitions/spirit-dark-black-religious-life 

More Than a Flower
JAN 30 2026 - APR 26 2026
Level 2 (L2), Explore More! Gallery
More than a Flower shares the fresh and fragrant beauty of live orchids and connects stories, scholarship and art to this extraordinary species. Explore the many ways orchids connect individuals, communities and nature. Through video demonstrations of orchid care and a daily interactive orchid discovery station, visitors will learn how to easily and properly care for their own orchids and more.
https://nmaahc.si.edu/explore/exhibitions/more-flower 

A Century in the Making
Permanent Exhibit (no end date)
Concourse Level (C)
A Century in the Making explores the journey to open the newest Smithsonian museum on the National Mall. This exhibition chronicles the century-long struggle, many attempts and numerous steps to realize the opening of the museumтАФincluding the activism of private citizens and organizations, passage of federal legislation, construction of an inspiring new building and collecting thousands of artifacts.
https://nmaahc.si.edu/explore/exhibitions/century-making 

At the Vanguard
JAN 16 2026 - JUL 19 2026
Concourse Level (C), Bank of America Special Exhibitions Gallery 
At the Vanguard weaves together stories of ingenuity, artistry and resistance тАФ through collections from Clark Atlanta University, Florida A&M University, Jackson State University, Texas Southern University and Tuskegee University. Explore stories of creativity, resilience, and legacy through rare collections of our five Historically Black Colleges and Universities partners. This exhibition celebrates how HBCUs preserve historyтАФand shape the future. Be where history lives. Join us at the vanguard.
https://nmaahc.si.edu/explore/exhibitions/vanguard 

A Changing America
Permanent Exhibit (no end date)
Concourse 1 (C1), History Galleries
A Changing America: 1968 and Beyond explores contemporary black life through stories about the social, economic, political, and cultural experiences of African Americans. This exhibition considers the challenges faced by African AmericansтАФchallenges compounded by experiences of class, gender, and immigrationтАФas they continue to fight for racial equity and social justice, issues as relevant to the 21st century as to the 20th. 
https://nmaahc.si.edu/explore/exhibitions/changing-america 

Defending Freedom, Defining Freedom
Permanent Exhibit (no end date)
Concourse 2 (C2), History Galleries
Defending Freedom, Defining Freedom: The Era of Segregation 1876-1968 captures the major aspects of that struggle and illustrates how African Americans not only survived the challenges set before them, but crafted an important role for themselves in the nation. The years after the Civil War were both hopeful and worrisome for African Americans. With the end of slavery, Black Americans had hoped to attain full citizenship. Instead, they found themselves resisting a new form of discriminationтАФsegregation.
https://nmaahc.si.edu/explore/exhibitions/defending-freedom-defining-freedom 

Slavery and Freedom
Permanent Exhibit (no end date)
Concourse 3 (C3), History Galleries
Slavery and Freedom explores the complex story of slavery and freedom, which rests at the core of our nationтАЩs shared history. Explore the history of slavery in the U.S. and the stories of African Americans whose struggles for freedom shaped the nation.
https://nmaahc.si.edu/explore/exhibitions/slavery-and-freedom

Basquiat x Banksy
SEP 29 2024 - SEP 7 2026
Lower Level
Basquiat ├Ч Banksy is an exhibition of two major paintings, one by Jean-Michel Basquiat (b. Brooklyn, New York, 1960тАУ1988) and the other by Banksy (anonymous; b. near Bristol, England). Placed in dialogue, BasquiatтАЩs Boy and Dog in a Johnnypump (1982) and BanksyтАЩs response, Banksquiat. Boy and Dog in Stop and Search (2018), reveal throughlines among street art, contemporary art, and the popular imagination.
Basquiat ├Ч Banksy marks the first time that artwork by either artist has been presented at the nationтАЩs museum of modern and contemporary art. The exhibition also includes 20 small works on paper and wood from the collection of Larry Warsh that were made by Basquiat between 1979 and 1985 and demonstrate the artistтАЩs deep familiarity with art history, his use of language, and his signature motifs, such as skulls and crowns. The film Downtown 81 (shot in 1980тАУ1981 and released in 2000), a send-up of the denizens of ManhattanтАЩs тАЩ80s avant-garde that stars Basquiat as a struggling artist named тАЬJean,тАЭ is also on view.
Accompanying public programs include a free hourlong lecture by Richard J. Powell, John Spencer Bassett Professor of Art and Art History at Duke University and a distinguished scholar of African American art and art of the African diaspora, at 6:30 PM on Oct. 10 in the HirshhornтАЩs Ring Auditorium.
https://hirshhorn.si.edu/exhibitions/basquiat-x-banksy/ 

Revolutions: Art from the Hirshhorn Collection, 1860-1960
MAR 22 2024 - NOV 1 2026 
Second Floor, Outer-Circle Galleries
In celebration of its 50th-anniversary season, the SmithsonianтАЩs Hirshhorn Museum presents Revolutions: Art from the Hirshhorn Collection, 1860тАУ1960, a major survey of artwork made during a transformative period characterized by new currents in science and philosophy and ever-increasing mechanization. Revolutions captures shifting cultural landscapes through the largely chronological presentation of 208 artworks made by 122 artistsтАФincluding Francis Bacon, Jean Dubuffet, Lee Krasner, Wilfredo Lam, Georgia OтАЩKeeffe, Pablo Picasso, and Jackson PollockтАФduring these turbulent and energetic years. Filling the Outer Ring galleries on the MuseumтАЩs second floor, the works are all part of the HirshhornтАЩs permanent collection, and many were gifts to the nation from founding donor Joseph H. Hirshhorn.
The exhibition also includes contemporary work by 19 artists in the permanent collection, including Abraham Cruzvillegas, Torkwase Dyson, Annette Lemieux, Joel Sternfeld, Hiroshi Sugimoto, Genesis Tramaine, and Flora Yukhnovich, whose practices demonstrate that many of the revolutionary ideas and approaches arising during these 100 years remain critical today.
Revolutions spotlights the rush of art-historical movements and genres that characterized both the arc of Modernism and the ascendancy of abstraction, notably through the work of artists interested in engaging the mind, not just the eye. This breadth was evident in Joseph HirshhornтАЩs founding gifts to the Museum. An industrialist, collector, and philanthropist, he donated nearly 6,000 worksтАФincluding a significant number of sculpturesтАФin anticipation of the MuseumтАЩs opening on October 4, 1974, and 6,400 more were gifted upon his death in 1981. Together these gifts constitute one of the most important collections of postwar American and European art in the world. Today the Hirshhorn collection comprises more than 13,130 artworks.
https://hirshhorn.si.edu/exhibitions/revolutions-art-from-the-hirshhorn-collection-1860-1960/ 

Adam Pendleton: Love, Queen 
APR 4 2025 - JAN 3 2027
Second Floor, Inner-Ring Galleries 
The Hirshhorn Museum presents Adam Pendleton: Love, Queen, a landmark exhibition of new and recent paintings, as well as a single-channel video work, in the MuseumтАЩs second-floor inner-ring galleries from April 4, 2025, to January 3, 2027. In his first solo exhibition in Washington, DC, Adam Pendleton highlights his unique contributions to contemporary American painting while making use of the architecture of the Museum and the history of the National Mall.
In its totality, Adam Pendleton: Love, Queen offers a powerful counterpoint to the MuseumтАЩs collection surveys that are concurrently presented in adjacent galleries.
https://hirshhorn.si.edu/exhibitions/adam-pendleton-love-queen/ 

Big Things for Big Rooms
DEC 20 2025 - JUL 4 2027
Second Floor galleries
Big Things for Big RoomsтАпtraces the development of immersive, large-scale artworks since the late 1960s. This presentation of 10 artworksтАФfive on view for the first time at the MuseumтАФis drawn largely from the Hirshhorn collection.  
Organized in two parts, the exhibition offers a multisensorial investigation of how artists create installation works that expand the boundaries of an artwork and the role of the visitor. The first part introduces the development of тАЬEnvironments,тАЭ expansive installations by pioneering artists such as Dan Flavin, Sam Gilliam, Robert Irwin (whose work defined the Light and Space movement), Lygia Pape, and Land artist Richard Long. The second half demonstrates the ways that contemporary artists such as Paul Chan, Olafur Eliasson, Spencer Finch, Rashid Johnson, and Mika Rottenberg are expanding upon these foundational ideas in different ways, often using everyday materials.тАп
https://hirshhorn.si.edu/exhibitions/big-things-for-big-rooms/ 

Mark Bradford: PickettтАЩs Charge 
NOV 8 2017 - ONGOING
Third Floor
Internationally renowned artist Mark Bradford (b. 1961) has debuted one of his largest works to date with PickettтАЩs Charge, a monumental new commission that spans nearly 400 linear feet.
PickettтАЩs Charge builds upon the HirshhornтАЩs continued commitment to showcasing the ways that artists respond to the unique political and cultural climate of their time. Through its free exhibitions and public programs, the Hirshhorn is dedicated to fostering conversation around the forces that shape creative expression in the twenty-first century.
https://hirshhorn.si.edu/exhibitions/mark-bradford-picketts-charge/ 

Barbara Kruger: Belief + Doubt 
AUG 20 2012 - ONGOING
Lower Level
Part of an initiative to bring art to new sites within and around the building, this installation by Barbara Kruger fills the Lower Level lobby and extends into the Museum bookstore. Famous for her incisive photomontages, Kruger has focused increasingly over the past two decades on creating environments that surround the viewer with language. The entire spaceтАФwalls, floor, escalator sidesтАФis wrapped in text-printed vinyl, immersing visitors in a spectacular hall of voices where words crafted by the artist or borrowed from the popular lexicon address conflicting perceptions of democracy, power, and belief.
At a moment when ideological certitude and purity seem especially valued, Kruger says sheтАЩs тАЬinterested in introducing doubt.тАЭ Large areas of the installation are devoted to open-ended questions (тАЬWHO IS BEYOND THE LAW? WHO IS FREE TO CHOOSE? WHO SPEAKS? WHO IS SILENT?тАЭ), while the section occupying the bookstore explores themes of desire and consumption. At once addressing the individual, the museum, and, symbolically, the country, KrugerтАЩs penetrating examination of the public sphere transforms one of the HirshhornтАЩs key public spaces.
https://hirshhorn.si.edu/exhibitions/barbara-kruger-beliefdoubt/ 

Laurie Anderson: Four Talks
ONGOING
Second Floor, Outer-Ring
Laurie Anderson is one of the leading multimedia artists of our time, and her innovative work in performance, music, technology, and visual art has profoundly influenced popular culture for more than forty years. In 2021, as part of The WeatherтАФher largest US exhibition to dateтАФthe Hirshhorn invited Anderson to create a new work on site. Anderson worked ten-hour days at the Museum for more than two weeks, painting directly on the walls and floors of this large gallery and covering nearly every inch with stories, song lyrics, jokes, and commentary on current events. Painting in a stream-of-consciousness manner without preparatory sketches, she created an enveloping and intensely personal installation that takes visitors on a journey through her mind. The installationтАЩs title, Four Talks (2021), refers to the four sculpturesтАФa raven, a parrot, a canoe, and a shelfтАФat its center, each accompanied by a pithy story or text passage. Monumentally scaled, conceptually rich, and visually captivating, Four Talks, currently on long-term view on the second-floor outer ring, represents a key achievement in AndersonтАЩs career.
https://hirshhorn.si.edu/exhibitions/laurie-anderson-four-talks/ 

Sculpture Garden 
CLOSED FOR REVITALIZATION 
With more than thirty works of art displayed year-round, the Hirshhorn MuseumтАЩs Sculpture Garden and Plaza offer visitors a contemplative haven in the heart of our nationтАЩs capital. Comprising nearly a fourth of Joseph HirshhornтАЩs initial gift, sculptures were and remain a critical aspect of the MuseumтАЩs identity, and the Garden, which opened with the Museum in 1974, provides the perfect setting for a collection of modern sculpture that, at the time, was said to be тАЬwithout parallel in the world.тАЭ
In addition to the outdoor galleries that make up the Sculpture Garden, the Plaza surrounding the Museum building affords ample space to exhibit more contemporary works.
Together, the two sites form a landscaped venue for some of the MuseumтАЩs most cherished works.
https://hirshhorn.si.edu/exhibitions/sculpture-garden-plaza/

	New Humans: Memories of the Future
	MAR 21 2026 - ONGOING
	Second, Third, and Fourth Floor
New Humans explores how technological developments have inspired evolving definitions ofтАпtheтАптАЬhuman.тАЭ New Humans: Memories of the Future will inaugurate the New MuseumтАЩs expanded building with an exploration of artistsтАЩ enduring preoccupation with what it means to be human in the face of sweeping technological changes. New Humans will trace a diagonal history of the twentieth and twenty-first centuries through the work of more than 200 international artists, writers, scientists, architects, and filmmakers, highlighting key moments when dramatic technological and social changes spurred new conceptions of humanity and new visions for its possible futures.	https://www.newmuseum.org/exhibition/new-humans-memories-of-the-future/

	Expanding the Walls: Making Connections Between Photography, History, and Community
	THROUGH JUN 8 2026 	
For a quarter of a century, Expanding the Walls: Making Connections Between Photography, History, and Community, envisioned by Sandra Jackson-Dumont, has fostered critical thinking, artistic expression, and community engagement among its teen participants. This exhibition, which marks the twenty-fifth anniversary of Expanding the Walls, features photographs across the programтАЩs years, offering a glimpse into the people, places, and moments that define a teenagerтАЩs world. As their camera may have evolvedтАФfirst from Polaroid, then to film, and now to digitalтАФeach photographer presents a distinct visual language shaped by the techniques and technologies of their time. Whether navigating self, family, or community, these young artists use their camera to capture adolescence in all its complexity and clarity. One of the programтАЩs signature elements is its focus on the archive of renowned Harlem photographer James Van Der Zee (1886тАУ1983). By studying Van Der ZeeтАЩs portraits of HarlemтАЩs Black community in the early twentieth century, teens gain a deeper understanding of the historical context that shaped their community and how photography can be a powerful tool for documenting cultural identity. 	
https://www.studiomuseum.org/exhibitions/expanding-the-walls-making-connections-between-photography-history-and-community 

	At an ArmтАЩs Length: Expanding the Walls 2025 
	JUL 29 2025 - JUL 30 2026	
	at an armтАЩs length: Expanding the Walls 2025 is an online exhibition that features photography by the fifteen artists in the 2025 cohort of the Studio Museum in HarlemтАЩs signature teen program, Expanding the Walls: Making Connections between Photography, History, and Community. This year marks the programтАЩs twenty-fifth anniversary.The phrase тАЬat an armтАЩs lengthтАЭ suggests both physical proximity and emotional reserve, a desire to be close, yet the need to distance oneself. The artists in this exhibition capture a cautious intimacy shaped by the bittersweet edges of adolescence, exploring what it means to be in community while choosing what to share and what to hold close.
https://www.studiomuseum.org/exhibitions/at-an-arms-length-expanding-the-walls-2025 

	From Now: A Collection in Context
	NOV 15 2025 - AUG 16 2026
	From Now: A Collection in Context is a dynamic, shifting installation of thematic exchanges drawn entirely from the Studio Museum in HarlemтАЩs collection and installed throughout the building. Featuring a call-and-response of regular rotations of works, the exhibition is organized in sections that will unfold and evolve over the course of the year. Altogether, the installation presents a plurality of voices and explores motifs that have preoccupied artists of African descent across generations.

With works from the nineteenth century appearing alongside those of the present, From Now demonstrates the myriad ways artworks from disparate times, locations, and genresтАФand the artists who make themтАФcan be in dialogue. Works that have rarely, if ever, been on view are displayed with those both newly acquired and long synonymous with the institution. The exhibition thus follows in the lineage of past collection shows committed to revealing the many perspectives, identities, and forms of art making by Black artists.тАп
	https://www.studiomuseum.org/exhibitions/permanent-collection 

	To Be a Place
	NOV 15 2025 - AUG 30 2026 
To celebrate the Studio Museum in HarlemтАЩs nearly sixty-year history, a visual timeline of historical documents, media, and programming ephemera will lay out a concise and detailed narrative of the Museum, from its former building on Fifth Avenue to its current spot on 125th Street. This installation will offer visitors an opportunity to discover the host of exhibitions, events, and programs that have defined the institution, and the communities with which it has engaged, throughout six decades of cultural, political, and societal change. 
	https://www.studiomuseum.org/exhibitions/studio-museum-archives 

	Christopher Myers: Harlem is a Myth
	ONGOING
	The Education Workshop are the first spaces dedicated to the Studio Museum in HarlemтАЩs education programs, where audiences of all ages engage with art in creative, collaborative, and dynamic ways. In honor of the Museum's commitment to such purpose-driven art education, artist Christopher Myers presents the site-specific installation, Harlem Is a Myth. Harlem Is a Myth depicts an intergenerational community of mythic beings, including figures from iconic moments in Harlem. Myers transforms a young Kareem Abdul-Jabbar into a basketball-carrying centaur, jazz legends Thelonious Monk and Count Basie sprout butterfly and angel wings, and two girls strike poses with antlers and a tail.

Harlem Is a Myth was also inspired by an encounter Myers experienced in Harlem nearly fifteen years ago while walking along 125th Street. A woman, unknown to the artist, approached him to say, тАЬI can tell you are an angel even though you donтАЩt know you have wings.тАЭ She described her ability to see what others cannot, and she insisted that people need to be loved despite тАЬthe little bit of monster on the inside.тАЭ Reflecting on this exchange, Myers says, тАЬAll of us have deep, inner stories to tell, and I was inspired to see what she saw, the whimsy and magic in all of us.тАЭ

Harlem Is a Myth invites all who enter the Education Workshop to consider what inner stories can be shared through art. How might these stories come to life when making art in community within the Museum and beyond? How can we use materials to explore and imagine worlds beyond our own?
https://www.studiomuseum.org/exhibitions/christopher-myers-harlem-is-a-myth 

	Camille Norment: Untitled (Heliotrope)
	ONGOING
	Commissioned by the Studio Museum in Harlem to create a site-informed work for its terrace staircase, Camille Norment presents Untitled (heliotrope), a sculptural and sound installation inspired by contemporary and historical migration. Handwoven by the artist herself, brass wires frame brass tubes of varying lengths and diameters; the resulting shape recalls both a pipe organ and a raft.  

The placement of NormentтАЩs work in the Studio MuseumтАФalong the wall of a passageway with a view toward the SouthтАФengages with diasporic migratory patterns from North to South and South to North caused by numerous sociopolitical, environmental, and cultural concerns. Untitled (heliotrope) positions тАЬsocial heliotropismтАЭтАФthe orientation toward perceived sources of growth and care during difficult circumstances, like sunflowers turning to the sunтАФas a framework to consider migration. As the installation suggests, the search for harmony amid dissonance is integral to the diasporic experience.
	https://www.studiomuseum.org/exhibitions/camille-norment-untitled-heliotrope 

	Kapwani Kiwanga: Bleed
	MAR 11 2026 - APR 1 2027
	BLEED is a new site-specific commission by French and Canadian artist Kapwani Kiwanga. Installed in the MuseumтАЩs second-floor project gallery and on view from March 11, 2026, until April 1, 2027, BLEED draws inspiration from quilting traditions and the symbolism embedded in their intricate designs.

Along the Underground Railroad, quilts hanging on clotheslines were believed to be stitched with codes that communicated critical information. BLEED features one of these motifsтАФa pattern of triangles called the тАЬflying geeseтАЭ that was purported to guide people north. Expanding on this encrypted language and Black traditions of knowledge sharing, Kiwanga transposes the pattern into black, blue, and crimson undulations. To achieve these colors, Kiwanga employed three distinct natural dye processes. Oxidizing pigment with salt water collected from the Atlantic Ocean produced the dappled black fabric. Through this blend of materials, Kiwanga references the transatlantic trade and engages the sea as a witness to and keeper of memories. The deep red circular shape comes from pokeberries, which are native to North America. Although they are known for their toxicity, pokeberries are often used as a dye for clothing and, when prepared correctly, for their medicinal properties. In 1816 a Black woman named Delphy was accused of poisoning her enslaver by feeding her pokeberries, an act of self-determination that inspired KiwangaтАЩs use of the fruit. Indigo dye provides the careening blue swells in the work. Cultivated using the forced labor of people under the condition of slavery who brought knowledge of the plant from West Africa, indigo fueled plantation economies in the South. In BLEED, indigo illuminates Black ancestral bonds and an inherited relationship to the land. Featuring fugitive dyes, which are colors that can shift over time, BLEED is imbued with an impermanence that allows the work to become a register of the passage of time.
	https://www.studiomuseum.org/exhibitions/kapwani-kiwanga-bleed

CURRENT
Agnes Martin: Painting is not making paintings 
APR 4 2026 - ONGOING 	
Agnes Martin: Painting is not making paintings draws primarily from DiaтАЩs extensive collection of MartinтАЩs canvases to focus on the breadth of the artistтАЩs output during the 1950s and тАЩ60s, complemented by important works from the latter decades of her practice, as well as significant loans. Charting MartinтАЩs transition from quasi-organic abstraction to the graphite grid, this selection illuminates how she developed her approach to creating highly considered, delicately balanced compositions, which progressed slowly and iteratively over time. Key examples of her use of the gridтАФa distinctly reduced compositional device, rigorously yet meditatively articulated with hand-drawn linesтАФdemonstrate how Martin expanded and refined her Minimal vocabulary over the course of the 1960s. A series of works created post-1974, following a painting hiatus of several years, encompass the range of compositions and palettes she adopted in that period, from horizontal bands and luminous acrylic washes to the return of geometric forms and her final тАЬblackтАЭ canvases. MartinтАЩs evolution over the course of five decades articulates her refusal of painting as a product-driven practice but as a way of existing in the world. Returning her work to Dia BeaconтАЩs galleries for the first time in nearly a decade, this exhibition offers a renewed opportunity to view MartinтАЩs singular contributions to Minimalism in the context of her conceptually like-minded peers.
https://www.diaart.org/exhibition/exhibitions-projects/agnes-martin-painting-is-not-making-paintings-exhibition/location/dia-beacon-beacon-united-states

Stanley Brouwn 
APR 15 2023 - MAY 18 2026	
this presentation coincides with stanley brouwn, the artistтАЩs first comprehensive solo exhibition in the united states, on view at the art institute of chicago april 8тАУjuly 31, 2023, and is co-curated by jordan carter and ann goldstein, the art institute's deputy director and chair and dittmer curator of modern and contemporary art.
https://www.diaart.org/exhibition/exhibitions-projects/stanley-brouwn-exhibition/location/dia-beacon-beacon-united-states 

Jack Whitten: Prime Mover
OCT 24 2025 - JUN 22 2026
Jack Whitten: Prime Mover brings together a group of recently acquired works on paper that Jack Whitten realized during the 1970s using a range of dry and wet black pigments. The year 1970 saw a shift in the artistтАЩs studio methods, with systematic process replacing the gestural abstraction of the previous decade. Moving away from the easel, he started to work horizontally on flat surfaces and employ new tools, materials, and methods of his own design to generate images that dispense with the artistтАЩs hand. In keeping with the language of contemporary technologies, Whitten began using the term тАЬdeveloped,тАЭ as opposed to тАЬdesigned,тАЭ to describe his changed approach to image making. Throughout the decade, as this presentation attests, the pulse of experimentation in WhittenтАЩs oeuvre was first felt on paper.
https://www.diaart.org/exhibition/exhibitions-projects/jack-whitten-prime-mover-exhibition/location/dia-beacon-beacon-united-states 

Larry Bell
Long-term view 
A leading figure of Southern CaliforniaтАЩs Light and Space movement, Larry Bell explores the intersections of light, color, and volume through glass. Since the early 1960s his experimentations with how visitors encounter his sculptures within an environment have included vacuum-coating his glass panels with metallic particles to create reflective and translucent surfaces and forms. This exhibition at Dia Beacon brings together a focused selection of BellтАЩs early sculptures from key small cubes to one of his first free-standing sculptures, Standing Walls (1968), now in DiaтАЩs collection. These will be presented alongside Duo Nesting Boxes (2021), a new diptych conceived for Dia that references both the open-form autonomy of BellтАЩs standing walls and the geometry of his signature cubes. In keeping with BellтАЩs most recent interests in the apparent saturation and density of color, Duo Nesting Boxes consists of layered panels of green and blue glass.
https://www.diaart.org/exhibition/exhibitions-projects/larry-bell-exhibition/location/dia-beacon-beacon-united-states 

Louise Bourgeois
Long-term view
тАЬEvery day,тАЭ Louise Bourgeois said, тАЬyou have to abandon your past or accept it, and then, if you cannot accept it, you become a sculptor.тАЭ For her, making art entails trying to translate experience into formтАФan operation that she compares with exorcism. In BourgeoisтАЩs works on view in these galleries, organic formations fuse with the inorganic materiality of the media in which they are rendered, be it marble, wood, or bronze. The artistтАЩs repertoire of materials spans traditional media and new textures, such as latex and synthetic resin. In her work, representation often entails the creation of a surrogate for the body and its suffering organs.
https://www.diaart.org/exhibition/exhibitions-projects/louise-bourgeois-exhibition/location/dia-beacon-beacon-united-states 

Ren├йe Green: The Equator Has Moved	
MAR 7 2025 - OCT 12 2026
Ren├йe Green: The Equator Has Moved marks the multidisciplinary artistтАЩs first major solo museum presentation in New York. Since the late 1980s, Green has produced densely layered, knowledge-based work that adapts strategies of Minimal and Conceptual art from the 1960s and тАЩ70s. In her uniquely recursive process, Green juxtaposes a range of materialsтАФarchival, documentary, and literary fragments; personal and found ephemera; speculative narratives; and her own extant workтАФto probe the unstable boundaries between fact and fiction, public recollection and personal memory.
https://www.diaart.org/exhibition/exhibitions-projects/renee-green-the-equator-has-moved-exhibition/location/dia-beacon-beacon-united-states 

Michael Heizer
Long-term view
Though Michael Heizer began his career as a painter, he is best known for the monumental sculptural works he began making in the 1960s. Deeply concerned with archaeology, ecology, and the natural landscape, he uses stone and steel as his primary materials. Often cutting into and expunging parts of the landscape, Heizer developed the concept of a тАЬnegative sculpture,тАЭ where the presence of the work of art is made palpable precisely through its material absence. 
https://www.diaart.org/exhibition/exhibitions-projects/michael-heizer-exhibition/location/dia-beacon-beacon-united-states 

Roni Horn 
Long-term view
Since the late 1970s, Roni Horn has developed an expansive practice encompassing drawing, photography, sculpture, installation, and text. Her works are discrete and multifaceted, yet they are unified by an abiding conceptual focus on questions of perception and the fluidity of identityтАФof the object and of oneselfтАФas conditioned by varying circumstances. While the examination of materialsтАЩ properties is a significant aspect of Minimalism, HornтАЩs work critiques the movementтАЩs notion of the autonomous art object, allowing human subjectivity to shape it. The work is the process of becoming; it happens in the encounter with the viewer, repeatedly. The selection on view exemplifies the artistтАЩs early exploration of how we experience of the physical reality of chosen mediaтАФforms, materiality, presenceтАФthrough nuanced spatial compositions. Key to the contingent nature of her work is the investigation of how a materialтАЩs presence is heightened and doubling as both a visual and conceptual approach. Elements in HornтАЩs work are reiterated, defining themselves through differences as well as varying distances from one another.
https://www.diaart.org/exhibition/exhibitions-projects/roni-horn-exhibition-362/location/dia-beacon-beacon-united-states 

Tehching Hsieh: Lifeworks 1978-1999
Long-term view
Following Tehching HsiehтАЩs gift of 11 career-defining works to Dia in 2024, Tehching Hsieh: Lifeworks 1978тАУ1999 is the first retrospective of the Taiwanese American artistтАЩs radical performances. The exhibition covers 1978 through 1999, a period in which Hsieh enacted his five iconic One Year Performances followed by Tehching Hsieh 1986тАУ1999 (Thirteen Year Plan). For each of the yearlong works, Hsieh lived locked in a wooden cage; punched a time clock in his studio every hour, on the hour; lived outside, navigating New YorkтАЩs streets without shelter; was tied to another artist, Linda Montano, by an eight-foot rope; and refrained entirely from making, viewing, reading about, or speaking of art, respectively. During HsiehтАЩs final and longest performance, the artist made art but withheld it from the public for 13 years. The exhibition is organized according to an architectural model, conceptualized by the artist over the course of a decade and adapted for Dia Beacon, that spatially conveys the time endured for each performance as well as in between them.
https://www.diaart.org/exhibition/exhibitions-projects/tehching-hsieh-lifeworks-19781999-exhibition/location/dia-beacon-beacon-united-states 

Robert Irwin, Beacon Project
Long-term view
Robert IrwinтАЩs design for Dia Beacon, Beacon Project (1999тАУ2003), is the artistтАЩs second collaboration with Dia Art Foundation, following Prologue: x183 (1998) and Excursus: Homage to the Square3 (1998/2015). Conceiving of Dia Beacon as a work of art in and of itself, Irwin made subtle interventions into the buildingтАЩs lighting and developed a symmetrical floorplan to ensure that the galleries are presented nonhierarchically and without a single overarching historical or chronological narrative. Specifically envisioned for the display of the works in DiaтАЩs collection, IrwinтАЩs design maintains the character of the original structureтАФwith the sole addition of an entry vestibuleтАФand ensures that Dia BeaconтАЩs expansive galleries are entirely lit by natural light.    
The artist envisioned the museum as a тАЬsequence of experiencesтАЭ including riding the linear corridor of the Metro North railway up the Hudson River from Grand Central Station in New York City and descending into Dia BeaconтАЩs parking lot. Taking BeaconтАЩs local horticulture and seasonal light conditionsтАФas well as the former Nabisco factoryтАЩs architectureтАФinto consideration, IrwinтАЩs design for the landscape surrounding Dia Beacon incorporates indigenous plants that bloom throughout the year. Considering the possible ambulatory paths one could take through the grounds, Irwin designed a garden on the museumтАЩs west side to serve as a bridge between otherwise unconnected parts of the building.
https://www.diaart.org/exhibition/exhibitions-projects/robert-irwin-beacon-project-exhibition/location/dia-beacon-beacon-united-states 

Donald Judd
Long-term view
On view in these galleries is a focused presentation of Donald JuddтАЩs iconic plywood works from the 1970s, which exemplify the artistтАЩs ability to produce exquisitely complex works by combining essential geometry and common industrial materials. Starting in the 1960s Judd determined a basic vocabulary of materials and forms that he would use throughout his practice, placing simple geometric boxes directly on the floor or spaced evenly along the wall. In forgoing the pedestal, he engages viewers in a bodily experience that happens in real time and space. Judd rejected traditional notions of craftsmanship in favor of an industrial production more true to the nature of his materials, delegating the fabrication of his objects to specialized technicians who followed instructions and sketches provided by the artist.
https://www.diaart.org/exhibition/exhibitions-projects/donald-judd-exhibition-85/location/dia-beacon-beacon-united-states 

On Kawara 
Long-term view
On Kawara was deeply concerned with the ways humans experience and record time. Kawara began his Today Series of paintings on January 4, 1966, and continued to work on them until his death in mid-2014. Adhering to a rigorous set of rules that he established, Kawara required that each painting be completed on the date depicted on its surface and in the language and grammar of the country in which it was completed. In addition to these formal conventions, the Today Series paintings are stored in handmade cardboard boxes along with a clipping from the local newspaper. Occasionally these boxes are exhibited, and particularly in earlier works, phrases or text from the clippings would form part of the title as well. Combining the individual with the universal, the Today Series is both a deeply personal journey (asserting that I was here on this day), but also the story of humanity and struggles experienced on a much larger scaleтАФas captured through the lens of daily newspaper reportage.
https://www.diaart.org/exhibition/exhibitions-projects/on-kawara-exhibition/location/dia-beacon-beacon-united-states 

Imi Knoebel 
Long-term view
Imi KnoebelтАЩs practice often centers on spatial relations in addition to the fundamentals of painting and sculpture, preoccupations he developed during his education at the Kunstakademie D├╝sseldorf studying under Joseph Beuys. In Raum 19 (Room 19, 1968), Knoebel reduces the core elements of a traditional artistic practiceтАФstretchers, picture frames, and various planar surfacesтАФto distill the essence of form, material, surface, space, and support. Room 19 can be variously arranged, depending on the context; since no fixed set of relationships binds the components, the work can expand to an environmental scale. Alternatively, it may be densely compacted as it would be in storage. As such, the form of the work becomes an event, contingent upon presentation and staging.
https://www.diaart.org/exhibition/exhibitions-projects/imi-knoebel-exhibition/location/dia-beacon-beacon-united-states 

Louise Lawler
Long-term view
Since the early 1970s, Louise Lawler has created works that expose the economic and social conditions that affect the reception of art. LawlerтАЩs work directs attention to positions of artistic authority and upends the presentation strategies that shape an encounter with an artwork.
https://www.diaart.org/exhibition/exhibitions-projects/louise-lawler-exhibition/location/dia-beacon-beacon-united-states 

Sol LeWitt 
Long-term view 
In the late 1960s, Sol LeWitt established a set of aesthetic principles through two key texts that would form the basis of his practice: тАЬParagraphs on Conceptual ArtтАЭ (1967) and тАЬSentences on Conceptual ArtтАЭ (1969). For LeWitt, тАЬthe idea or concept is the most important aspect of the work.тАЭ He began to use these ideas as guidelines for two-dimensional works drawn directly on the wall. LeWittтАЩs outlook and practice inaugurated a new genre that he would explore for the remainder of his career.
The wall drawings are the result of a set of instructions that are normally brief and relatively direct; consequently, their results vary in complexity and scale.  тАЬParagraphs on Conceptual ArtтАЭ emphasized this level of preparedness. LeWitt asserted that тАЬall of the planning and decisions are made beforehand and the execution is a perfunctory affair.тАЭ Although the earliest of these works were drawn by LeWitt, the series quickly grew into a form of visual score that could be better interpreted by a qualified assistant or group of assistants in a specific location.
https://www.diaart.org/exhibition/exhibitions-projects/sol-lewitt-exhibition/location/dia-beacon-beacon-united-states 

Max Neuhaus 
Long-term view
A pioneer in the field of contemporary art and music, Max Neuhaus is credited with being the first artist to use sound as a medium for site-specific installations. His sound installations allow listeners to approach sound as art, in their own time. Testing the idea that our perception of a place depends also on what we hear, Neuhaus extended sound into social spaces to create sites altered by the synthetic, anonymous sounds concealed within them. Commissioned by Dia in 2005, Time Piece Beacon is based on the principle of a тАЬsound signal in reverse,тАЭ a subtle sound that is noticed when it disappears rather than when it begins. As each hour approaches, a low tone gradually emerges along the perimeters of the galleries at Dia Beacon, and the hour is signaled when the sound abruptly ends.
https://www.diaart.org/exhibition/exhibitions-projects/max-neuhaus-exhibition/location/dia-beacon-beacon-united-states 

H├йlio Oiticica 
Long-term view
H├йlio Oiticica was a groundbreaking visual artist and theorist whose diverse practice spanned sculpture, drawing, painting, installation, and performance. His expansive body of work laid the foundations for participatory art, offering radical insights into abstraction through the lens of social, political, and economic conditions in Latin America and beyond. As a central figure in BrazilтАЩs Neoconcrete movement and a co-founder of the Tropic├бlia movement, OiticicaтАЩs innovative approach emphasized the importance of spatial awareness and embodied interaction. At Dia Beacon, rare works on canvas from the artistтАЩs Metaesquemas (Meta-Schemes, 1958тАУ59) and Relevos Espaciais (Spatial Reliefs, 1959) series are on display alongside the large-scale Grande N├║cleo (Grand Nucleus) (1960тАУ66), which stands out as one of OiticicaтАЩs most engaging environments. Breaking with the two-dimensional boundaries of his earlier works, Grande N├║cleo was created as a complex structure of hanging rectangular panels, painted in a vibrant spectrum from bright yellow to deep orange, and arranged in a dynamic grid of varying angles and heights. Across the exhibition, the viewerтАЩs corporeal presence, movement, and perception of time and space are activated, underscoring OiticicaтАЩs evolving exploration of structure, color, and spatial engagement.
https://www.diaart.org/exhibition/exhibitions-projects/helio-oiticica-exhibition/location/dia-beacon-beacon-united-states 

Gerhard Richter
Long-term view
Gerhard Richter realized Six Gray Mirrors as a site-specific work for Dia Beacon in 2003. Six gray-enameled glass panels hang from the walls on supports that allow them to be tilted at various angles. Their neutral depths not only reflect visitors but also respond to the light from the high windows, combining architecture, sculpture, and painting into a synthetic whole. The somber appearance of the work simultaneously negates and combines RichterтАЩs passion for glass, mirror, and monochromeтАФthree tenets in the tradition of painting that the artist engaged throughout his career.
https://www.diaart.org/exhibition/exhibitions-projects/gerhard-richter-exhibition/location/dia-beacon-beacon-united-states 

Robert Ryman 
Long-term view
In the late 1960s, Robert Ryman observed that тАЬthere is never a question of what to paint, but only how to paint.тАЭ On long-term view since Dia Beacon opened in 2003, these galleries uniquely represent the range of techniques that Ryman pursued throughout his career. His paintings vary broadly, from gestural to self-effacing, pristine to vigorously layered, loosely brushed to delicately applied. His repertoire of materials is just as assorted, including various types of industrial paints and rare pigments, supports, adhesives, and fixtures such as fiberglass, steel, aluminum, and wood.
Originally trained as a jazz saxophonist, Ryman turned to painting after he began working as a guard at the Museum of Modern Art in 1953. He received little in the way of formal artistic training but devoted himself to studying painting through hands-on experimentation. RymanтАЩs earliest works from the late 1950s and early 1960s demonstrate an intense interest in the quality of paint and in the surfaces he built up through varied facture. Belying his reputation as a painter solely interested in white, Ryman explored the relationship between chromatic and achromatic tones. Many of his paintings from the 1980s expand into the viewerтАЩs space, either through unconventional support structures or materials, and challenge the standard interaction between viewer and artwork.
https://www.diaart.org/exhibition/exhibitions-projects/robert-ryman-exhibition-94/location/dia-beacon-beacon-united-states 

Lucas Samaras
Long-term view
For over 60 years, Lucas Samaras worked fluidly between mediums in a manner that eluded categorization. The artistтАЩs eccentric and uncanny objects often combine formal strategies of Minimalism with the haptic materiality of everyday objects. Such is the case with Cubes and Trapezoids (1994тАУ95), which joined the collection in 2003 and will be presented at Dia Beacon for the first time since its 1994 debut at Pace Gallery in New York, together with a significant loan of one of the artistтАЩs immersive mirrored rooms, Doorway (1966/2007).
The cubes consist of 24 totemic wooden volumes, covered in pale gray Nevamar laminate with cutouts of various geometrical shapes, that are arranged in an expansive grid. A material index of SamarasтАЩs move to a new high-rise apartment building featuring the same gray surface treatment, the sculptures merge the vocabulary of the Minimal cube with elements drawn from the artistтАЩs domestic architecture and autobiography. The related wall-works, the trapezoids, are made up of eight irregular quadrilateral forms nestled within uniform rectangles. The non-reflective surfaces of the laminated and latex-painted trapezoids, which nonetheless respond to light, complement the mirrored panels of Doorway. Together these psychologically charged objects literally and materially evoke the body, perverting the analytical geometries of Minimalism with the messy realities of identity and interiority.
https://www.diaart.org/exhibition/exhibitions-projects/lucas-samaras-exhibition/location/dia-beacon-beacon-united-states 

Richard Serra
Long-term view
Richard Serra has consistently and rigorously probed issues fundamental to sculpture over a career now spanning nearly six decades. In the late 1960s he introduced тАЬprocessтАЭ into his sculptural practice by making explicit the means of his production. Between 1967 and 1968 Serra penned a list of transitive verbs, which he applied to new and innovative materials to make sculptures. SerraтАЩs Scatter Piece (1968) is an example of this, consisting of rubber strips randomly distributed throughout the gallery. SerraтАЩs work is on long-term view across five galleries at Dia Beacon.
Throughout his career, SerraтАЩs work engaged with тАЬways of relating movement to material and space.тАЭ These concerns remained central to the steel sculptures he made in the 1990s and early 2000s. Ranging from Elevation Wedge (2001), a ramp that subtly inclines the floor of the gallery, to his monumental Torqued Ellipses series, these large installations of contorted steel plates elaborate concerns with orientation and movement, destabilizing our experience of space as we attempt to comprehend each sculptural volume. They are part of SerraтАЩs investigation into the embodied experience of perception.
https://www.diaart.org/exhibition/exhibitions-projects/richard-serra-exhibition/location/dia-beacon-beacon-united-states 

Robert Smithson 
Long-term view
On view in these galleries are five of Robert SmithsonтАЩs indoor earthworks from the late 1960s, made with materials such as sand, gravel, mirrors, and glass. Deeply informed by science in its popularized formsтАФsuch as science fiction literature and cinema, encyclopedic collections, and natural history museumsтАФhis practice addresses processes of accumulation, displacement, and entropy in order to reveal the contradictions in our visible world.
Smithson focused his short but influential career on a reconsideration of sculpture in relation to nature. He began his career as a painter but in the mid-1960s started experimenting with different media including sculpture, writing, drawing, film, and eventually, earthworks. Sometimes the results were fleeting documentations, other times permanent, large-scale sculptural interventionsтАФas in the case of Spiral Jetty (1970), the iconic earthwork maintained by Dia on the northeastern shore of Great Salt Lake, Utah.
https://www.diaart.org/exhibition/exhibitions-projects/robert-smithson-exhibition/location/dia-beacon-beacon-united-states 

Keith Sonnier 
Long-term view
Since the mid-1960s, Keith Sonnier seamlessly integrated an array of media into his practice while prioritizing concept, process, and duration. This presentation marks the artistтАЩs first posthumous institutional exhibition in the United States, featuring a group of works realized between 1968 and 1970. During this formative period the artist radically reconsidered the haptic, spatial, and temporal dynamics of sculpture: from what he referred to as his тАЬfloor-to-wallтАЭ sculptures to installations that envelop their architectural surroundings with light and color. In these works, Sonnier pursued what he termed тАЬpsychologically loadedтАЭ industrial materialsтАФincluding cloth and satin in addition to neon, latex, and flockingтАФwith strong associative qualities. Many realized in situ, the sculptures and installations on view reconstitute the pivotal, early years of SonnierтАЩs practice, encapsulating foundational concerns and innovative strategies that defined his artistic vocabulary, including the entanglement of material, light, time, and space, as well as the cultivation of psychological and sensual evocations through process and form. 
https://www.diaart.org/exhibition/exhibitions-projects/keith-sonnier-exhibition/location/dia-beacon-beacon-united-states 

Kishio Suga
Long-term view 
Kishio Suga brings together a representative group of the artistтАЩs sculptures, dating from the 1960s to the тАЩ90s, that probe the slippages between seeing and knowing. Works culled from DiaтАЩs holdings are complemented by key loans, together unsettling habitual expectations of materialsтАЩ behaviors, including concrete, machine oil, paraffin wax, metal, and stone that are set in serial, mutually upholding, and at times precarious arrangements. Inflected anew by the conditions of the site in which they are displayed, each of SugaтАЩs sculptures stages a carefully framed incoherence.
In conjunction with the exhibitionтАЩs opening, SugaтАЩs murder-mystery film, Being and Murder (1999), and video documentation of his performative тАЬactivationsтАЭ will screen for the first time outside of Japan at Dia Chelsea, from July 9 to August 9.
https://www.diaart.org/exhibition/exhibitions-projects/kishio-suga-exhibition-354/location/dia-beacon-beacon-united-states 

Andy Warhol: Shadows 
CLOSING JUL 6 2026 
Andy WarholтАЩs Shadows (1978тАУ79) returns to Dia Beacon for long-term view in December 2023. A single painting in multiple parts, Shadows is one of WarholтАЩs most abstract works, yet one that cohesively synthesizes key elements of his practice, including film, painting, photography, and screenprinting. Originally commissioned by Dia and acquired in 1979 for a solo exhibition at 393 West Broadway in New York, Shadows includes a total of 102 canvases; the final number of canvases on view in each installation is determined by the dimensions of an existing exhibition space. 
https://www.diaart.org/exhibition/exhibitions-projects/andy-warhol-shadows-exhibition-303/location/dia-beacon-beacon-united-states 

Lawrence Weiner
Long-term view
Language is a dominant aspect of Lawrence WeinerтАЩs practice. Conceived as objective representations of states or processes rather than material realities, WeinerтАЩs works are capable of countless manifestations. Although their content is general and abstract, they remain inseparable from their presentation and context. These works could be defined as site-related; they are conceived in relation to the venue and circumstance. Whether the letters are stenciled, painted, or mounted in relief, the choice of typeface, size, placement, and color, varies with the site. The context serves as a vital factor for WeinerтАЩs works. A poster, artistтАЩs book, gallery, or public arena molds the workтАЩs meaning.
Various and versatile, WeinerтАЩs works at Dia Beacon remain dispersive. Visitors interact with them among the sculpture galleries, in a stairwell, and in the caf├й/bookshop. Suspended high over the admissions desk, the artistтАЩs Statement of Intent (1969) attests to his belief that тАЬart always institutionalizes itself,тАЭ regardless of placement. Such an active arrangement emphasizes the work of art is completed only through a viewerтАЩs potential reception and adoption.
https://www.diaart.org/exhibition/exhibitions-projects/lawrence-weiner-exhibition/location/dia-beacon-beacon-united-states

Noah Davis 
THROUGH APR 26 2026
Main Building, Morgan, Korman, and Field Galleries 150-155
Noah Davis began with a humble aspiration: тАШto represent the people around meтАЩ. Born in Seattle in 1983, he made LA his chosen home, where he worked to capture the intricacies of contemporary Black life with tenderness and depth. Beloved as a painter, this major retrospective presents other aspects of his practice too тАУ from collecting photography from flea markets to making collages, websites, sculpture and eventually his own museum.
The exhibition is making its final stop at The Philadelphia Museum of Art on an international tour organized with DAS MINSK in Potsdam, the Barbican in London, and the Hammer Museum in Los Angeles. Highlights will include 40 Acres and a Unicorn (2007), a striking blend of fantasy and history; Isis (2009), a portrait of his wife Karon depicted as the Egyptian goddess; Savage Wilds (2012), a series in which Davis cast his gaze upon the complex portrayals of Black subjects on daytime television; and the renowned Pueblo del Rio series (2014), paintings that reimagine one of the oldest, largest, and most architecturally significant public housing developments in Los Angeles.

https://www.philamuseum.org/exhibitions/noah-davis 


	Where Are We Now?: American People and Places, 1955-2025
	THROUGH APR 26 
	Main Building, Honickman Galleries 156, 157
	The installation Where Are We Now? American Places and People, 1955-2025 begins with photographs taken by Swiss-born artist Robert Frank, who, in 1955, published his book The Americans, comprised of photographs he made on an extended road trip across the United States. The book was controversial because of the almost offhand way it revealed the fissures in our national life, particularly the racism and other biases that shaped public experience.

Although FrankтАЩs photographs unsettled many citizens, his book was something of a love letter to his adopted country. This exhibition follows his spirit and surveys photographs made by many artists who probe American experience and identity in one way or another. The question in the installation title is open-ended. The photographs on view donтАЩt offer a simple answer. Taken together, they bring us to yet another simple question: what does it look like when we try to stick together?
	https://www.philamuseum.org/exhibitions/where-are-we-now 

	In Her View
THROUGH MAY 18 2026
Main Building, Korman Galleries 221-223
This exhibition celebrates the remarkable paintings, drawings, and prints by women artists in the Keith and Jim Straw collection. The local Philadelphia couple began collecting art in the 1970s, when it was still relatively unusual to focus a collection on women artists. They initially pursued works by artists active in the 1800s, but over time their collection expanded to include living makers with whom the pair often built personal relationships. In celebration of the promised gift of works from the Straw collection to the Philadelphia Museum of Art, this exhibition features notable works by Lilly Martin Spencer, Suzanne Valadon, Betye Saar, Jaune Quick-to-See Smith, and Kay WalkingStick, among others. Together, these artworks celebrate the resilience and creativity of women artists through time.
https://www.philamuseum.org/exhibitions/in-her-view-straw-collection

	Fantastical Creatures of Asia 
	ONGOING
	Main Building, Galleries 320 and 321
	Fantastical Creatures of Asia brings together works that explore how artists across time and region have imagined the supernatural to express cultural values, spiritual beliefs, and contemporary concerns.

	Julie Mehretu: In Focus
	THROUGH MAY 10 
	Main Building, Colket Gallery 251
	The museum recently acquired two monumental print series, Treatises on the Executed (from RobinтАЩs Intimacy) and This Manifestation of Historical Restlessness (from RobinтАЩs Intimacy) тАУ each fourteen-feet-long and comprised of ten panels printed from the same fifty copper plates. The works are the result of an intensive and multi-year collaboration between Mehretu and Case Hudson, veteran printer at the LA-based printmaking workshop, Gemini G.E.L, along with a team of etchers. Initiated during MehretuтАЩs residency at the workshop in 2019, the prints are as complex and intricate in technique as they are in imagery: made through a combination of etching and aquatint and inked in the ├а la poup├йe manner, a technique that involves hand-applying ink to selective etched areas of a plate and then expertly wiping it away from other areas. Together, the works showcase the high velocity of Mehretu in action: her bold, calligraphic marks, her insistent lines and notations that never fully disclose their meanings.
	https://www.philamuseum.org/exhibitions/julie-mehretu-in-focus 

	Visions of the Land in Japan 
	THROUGH JUL 1 
	Main Building, Gallery 342 
	Representing the land we live in is a practice shared across the world. In Japan, artists created a large body of landscape imagery that ranged from indigenous yamato-style depictions to portrayals of nature that incorporated Chinese and later Euro-American ideas and techniques.
When Zen Buddhist monks introduced Chinese ink painting to Japan around 1300, the new art form offered a fresh approach. Chinese paintings became prized collectibles for Buddhist temples and for the ruling class, and served as indispensable models for Japanese artists who aspired to master painting with ink and brush.
Over the centuries that followed, Japanese artists developed singular visions of their land, which encompassed idealized, imaginary views and true-to-life renditions. More influences arrived in the 1550s through encounters with Euro-American art, providing another source of inspiration for these artistsтАЩ expanding horizons.
Drawing from the collection, including some recent gifts, the museum here presents Japanese paintings and ceramics that span more than five hundred yearsтАФfrom 1500s to the present. These works not only showcase the evolution and expansion of artistic expressions of the land in Japan but also supply glimpses into JapanтАЩs shifting cultural and social landscapes.
	https://www.philamuseum.org/exhibitions/visions-of-the-land-edo-japan

	Collection Highlight: Ceremonial Teahouse
	ONGOING
	SmithKline Beecham Gallery 344, 3rd floor
	The name of this teahouse, Sunkaraku (Evanescent Joys), reflects the spirit of the traditional Japanese tea ceremony as a temporary refuge from the complexities of daily life. The architecture reveals a special delight in natural materials, such as bamboo and cedar.
Using elements from an eighteenth-century teahouse, ┼Мgi Rod┼Н designed this retreat around 1917 for the grounds of his Tokyo home. Among the guests he hosted at Sunkaraku were Japanese financial and political leaders for whom he designed country homes and teahouses. Acquired by the museum from the architect in 1928, this is the only example of his work outside Japan. It is still used for tea ceremonies on special occasions.
https://www.philamuseum.org/exhibitions/collection-highlight-ceremonial-teahouse 

	Collection Highlight: Temple Hall
	ONGOING
	Caplan Gallery 324, 3rd floor
	Debuting to the public in the museumтАЩs original home at Memorial Hall in 1920, the mandapam opened at its current location in 1940. Although a reconstruction, it incorporates many original architectural elements and provides visitors with a unique opportunity to experience the extraordinary synthesis of sculpture, architecture, and symbol that characterizes South IndiaтАЩs elaborate temple form.

	Frida: The Making of an Icon
	THROUGH MAY 17 2026 
	Caroline Wiess Law Building
	Frida KahloтАЩs art has resonated with millions of individuals around the globe. This exhibition tells the story of how she became one of the worldтАЩs most influential artists. 
Devoted to Frida KahloтАЩs life and legacy, Frida: The Making of an Icon premieres at the MFAH in January 2026. This monumental exhibition features more than 30 works by the legendary Mexican artist and 120 by five generations of artists she inspired.
Practically unknown to mainstream audiences during her lifetime (1907тАУ1954), Kahlo has been enshrined since the mid-1970s as the only female artist whose instant audience recognition and mass appeal rival those of male artists Vincent van Gogh, Pablo Picasso, and Andy Warhol.
Since the 1980s, retrospective exhibitions around the world have explored KahloтАЩs artistic production and contributions to 20th-century Modernism. By contrast, Frida: The Making of an Icon is the first major exploration of the artistтАЩs transformation from a relatively unknown local painter to a universal icon and global brand. Departing from the traditional retrospective format, the exhibition revolves around a selection of KahloтАЩs masterworks, memorabilia, and documents from her archives, as well as a vast array of works from artists across artistic and social movements who were inspired by her practice. A special gallery addresses the status of KahloтАЩs legacy as a pop-culture figure.
	https://www.mfah.org/art/exhibitions/frida-the-making-of-an-icon 

	Ernesto Neto: SunForceOceanLife
	THROUGH SEP 7 2026
	Caroline Wiess Law Building
	Engage with art like never before through hands-on exploration of this installation made especially for the Museum of Fine Arts, Houston. 
 
Returning to the MuseumтАЩs vast Cullinan Hall this spring and summer, Ernesto Neto: SunForceOceanLife is a soaring crochet installation that fills the space with spiraling color and movement. A major MFAH commission by renowned Brazilian artist Ernesto Neto, SunForceOceanLife suspends visitors some 12 feet in the air as they navigate an interior network of hand-woven passages.
 
Rooted in a crochet technique passed down from NetoтАЩs grandmother, the work merges craft traditions with contemporary practice. As part of the MuseumтАЩs ongoing engagement with Latin American art, Ernesto Neto: SunForceOceanLife joins a lineage of immersive installations that connect viewers to ideas of ecology, spirituality, and sensory awareness.
	https://www.mfah.org/art/exhibitions/ernesto-neto-sunforceoceanlife-26 

	Buddha / Nature: Five Dialogues on Our Shared World
	THROUGH MAY 10 2026
	Audrey Jones Beck Building
	Highlighting the connection between spiritual forms and the natural world through the millennia, the exquisite works in this exhibition bring Buddhist ideals to bear in the present.
 
Buddha / Nature: Five Dialogues on Our Shared World traces a path through Buddhist wisdom using both ancient sculpture and contemporary art to illuminate the ecological and ethical questions of our time. Five remarkable works from the Xuzhou Collection, on long-term loan to the Museum since 2021, anchor the exhibition and appear for the first time in a fully contemporary setting at the MFAH.
 
The exhibition unfolds across five galleries, each with a unique focus:
 
Samsara introduces the interwoven cycles of life through Beverly PennтАЩs new commission Samsara, made from invasive plants cast in bronze and paired with the 12th-century Tibetan Wisdom Buddha.


Impermanence brings together Hiroshi SugimotoтАЩs Mount FujiтАФa sweeping image of dawn on twin folding screensтАФwith a meditating Buddha from ancient Gandhara, evoking the fragile balance between permanence and sudden change.


Karma examines historical reckoning through a 6th-century terracotta Buddha flanked by works from Cannupa Hanska Luger and Erick Swenson, two distinct visions of humanityтАЩs relationship with nature.


Compassion pairs a Chinese Buddha triad with Liu XiaodongтАЩs large-scale portraits of families and migrants, extending empathy across social, cultural, and ecological boundaries.


Awakening concludes the exhibition with Beili Liu stitching red thread in the Arctic Circle, her patient gestures mirrored by an 8th-century Buddha head whose power endures even in fragment.
The timeless sculptures from the Xuzhou Collection were created as touchstones to something greater, links between humanity and the divine. In Buddha / Nature, that mediating force turns toward the present, inviting visitors to reflect, recalibrate, and consider the part each of us plays in shaping a world in flux.
	https://www.mfah.org/art/exhibitions/buddhanature

	Peter Bradley and тАЬThe De Luxe ShowтАЭ
	THROUGH MAY 31 2026
	Caroline Wiess Law Building
	View both historic and contemporary works from the artists included in Peter Bradley's The De Luxe Show, the landmark 1971 exhibition in Houston's Fifth Ward that committed to crossing racial lines and bringing тАЬfirst-rate art to people who donтАЩt usually attend shows."  

Peter Bradley (born 1940) worked at the center of elite art circles in the 1960s and 1970s as an associate director at New YorkтАЩs Perls Galleries. A noted member of the Color Field avant-garde, Bradley built his paintings upon nuanced chromatic harmonies. In 1971, at the invitation of John and Dominique de Menil, Bradley curated The De Luxe Show, one of the first racially integrated exhibitions of contemporary art in the United States. Opening in August of that year at the De LUXE Theater in HoustonтАЩs Fifth Ward, the exhibition presented both internationally recognized and emerging artists, promoting abstraction and crossing racial lines in an era defined by sweeping social upheaval. 
Alongside BradleyтАЩs signature canvases from the early 1970s and two recent lithographs that demonstrate his continued creative exploration, Peter Bradley and тАЬThe De Luxe ShowтАЭ includes works by Anthony Caro, Sam Gilliam, and Larry Poons. All four artists were shown in the original exhibition and shared pioneering practices: freeing sculpture from pedestal, canvas from stretcher, and paint from brush.
	https://www.mfah.org/art/exhibitions/peter-bradley-and-the-de-luxe-show 
	
	Art, Place, and Power: Project Row Houses in HoustonтАЩs Third Ward
	THROUGH NOV 8 2026
	Audrey Jones Beck Building 
	Learn more about the founding members of Project Row Houses, one of Houston's leading community-oriented arts organizations.
 
In 1993, seven Black artists transformed a block of abandoned row houses in HoustonтАЩs Third Ward neighborhood into a new kind of cultural space. Rather than regarding the structures as ruins of the past, these visionaries saw in them the foundation of something new. Believing that creativity and collective action could reshape both the built environment and peopleтАЩs lives, the artists established Project Row Houses, an arts and community revitalization organization that for over three decades has staged free exhibitions, offered artist residencies and youth programs, promoted the preservation of historic architecture, and more. 
 
The installation Art, Place, and Power: Project Row Houses in HoustonтАЩs Third Ward features works on paper by founders of Project Row Houses, including James Bettison, Bert Long, Jr., Jesse Lott, Rick Lowe, and Floyd Newsum, and is shown in conjunction with Textiles in Dialogue: The Design Works of Bedford Stuyvesant. Like the nearby textiles produced in BrooklynтАЩs Bedford-Stuyvesant neighborhood, these works celebrate the powerful impact of community-oriented artists and art.
https://www.mfah.org/art/exhibitions/art-place-and-power-project-row-houses-in-houstons-third-ward 
	
	Yayoi Kusama тАЬAftermath of Obliteration of EternityтАЭ
	THROUGH WINTER 2027
	Nancy and Rich Kinder Building
	Yayoi Kusama (Japanese, born 1929) was living in New York when she created her first Infinity Room in 1965. Kusama returned to Japan in 1970, and subsequent works became increasingly personal. When you visit this installation, you are invited to step into the room and stand on the central platform. Over time, a delicate, shimmering mirage unfolds, as lights ignite and are mirrored on every surface. In less than a minute, however, all light disappearsтАФand then the cycle starts anew.

	The Jewelry of Dorothea Pr├╝hl 
	THROUGH JAN 3 2027
	Nancy and Rich Kinder Building 
	A celebration of sculptural form and material mastery, The Jewelry of Dorothea Pr├╝hl marks the first U.S. exhibition dedicated to the German artist. Spanning nearly five decades of her work, this presentation features a series of necklaces and brooches that exemplify Dorothea Pr├╝hlтАЩs visionary approach to contemporary jewelry.
Internationally recognized for her bold, expressive forms crafted in wood and metal, Pr├╝hl (born 1937) trained in the traditions of the Bauhaus. Her expressive compositions and seemingly simple gestures belie a complexity and degree of craftsmanship that is unmatched in contemporary practice. Pr├╝hl attended the Burg Giebichenstein University of Art and Design in Halle, Germany, and returned to lead its jewelry and metalsmithing department for many years. In addition to shaping her own body of work, Pr├╝hl influenced generations of artists through her long career as a teacher and mentor. 
Comprised of necklaces and brooches dating from 1976 to 2025, The Jewelry of Dorothea Pr├╝hl is the result of an extraordinary gift from the Rotasa Collection Trust. The MFAH now holds the largest public collection of Pr├╝hlтАЩs jewelry in the world.
